\DoxyCodeLine{36 \textcolor{comment}{// Type utilities needed for implementing typed and type-\/parameterized}}
\DoxyCodeLine{37 \textcolor{comment}{// tests.  This file is generated by a SCRIPT.  DO NOT EDIT BY HAND!}}
\DoxyCodeLine{38 \textcolor{comment}{//}}
\DoxyCodeLine{39 \textcolor{comment}{// Currently we support at most 50 types in a list, and at most 50}}
\DoxyCodeLine{40 \textcolor{comment}{// type-\/parameterized tests in one type-\/parameterized test case.}}
\DoxyCodeLine{41 \textcolor{comment}{// Please contact googletestframework@googlegroups.com if you need}}
\DoxyCodeLine{42 \textcolor{comment}{// more.}}

\DoxyCodeLine{60 \textcolor{comment}{// GetTypeName<T>() returns a human-\/readable name of type T.}}
\DoxyCodeLine{61 \textcolor{comment}{// NB: This function is also used in Google Mock, so don't move it inside of}}
\DoxyCodeLine{62 \textcolor{comment}{// the typed-\/test-\/only section below.}}
\DoxyCodeLine{63 \textcolor{keyword}{template} <\textcolor{keyword}{typename} T>}
\DoxyCodeLine{64 std::string GetTypeName() \{}
\DoxyCodeLine{65 \textcolor{preprocessor}{\# if GTEST\_HAS\_RTTI}}
\DoxyCodeLine{66 }
\DoxyCodeLine{67   \textcolor{keyword}{const} \textcolor{keywordtype}{char}* \textcolor{keyword}{const} name = \textcolor{keyword}{typeid}(T).name();}
\DoxyCodeLine{68 \textcolor{preprocessor}{\#  if GTEST\_HAS\_CXXABI\_H\_ || defined(\_\_HP\_aCC)}}
\DoxyCodeLine{69   \textcolor{keywordtype}{int} status = 0;}
\DoxyCodeLine{70   \textcolor{comment}{// gcc's implementation of typeid(T).name() mangles the type name,}}
\DoxyCodeLine{71   \textcolor{comment}{// so we have to demangle it.}}
\DoxyCodeLine{72 \textcolor{preprocessor}{\#   if GTEST\_HAS\_CXXABI\_H\_}}
\DoxyCodeLine{73   \textcolor{keyword}{using} abi::\_\_cxa\_demangle;}
\DoxyCodeLine{74 \textcolor{preprocessor}{\#   endif  }\textcolor{comment}{// GTEST\_HAS\_CXXABI\_H\_}}
\DoxyCodeLine{75   \textcolor{keywordtype}{char}* \textcolor{keyword}{const} readable\_name = \_\_cxa\_demangle(name, 0, 0, \&status);}
\DoxyCodeLine{76   \textcolor{keyword}{const} std::string name\_str(status == 0 ? readable\_name : name);}
\DoxyCodeLine{77   free(readable\_name);}
\DoxyCodeLine{78   \textcolor{keywordflow}{return} name\_str;}
\DoxyCodeLine{79 \textcolor{preprocessor}{\#  else}}
\DoxyCodeLine{80   \textcolor{keywordflow}{return} name;}
\DoxyCodeLine{81 \textcolor{preprocessor}{\#  endif  }\textcolor{comment}{// GTEST\_HAS\_CXXABI\_H\_ || \_\_HP\_aCC}}
\DoxyCodeLine{82 }
\DoxyCodeLine{83 \textcolor{preprocessor}{\# else}}
\DoxyCodeLine{84 }
\DoxyCodeLine{85   \textcolor{keywordflow}{return} \textcolor{stringliteral}{"{}<type>"{}};}
\DoxyCodeLine{86 }
\DoxyCodeLine{87 \textcolor{preprocessor}{\# endif  }\textcolor{comment}{// GTEST\_HAS\_RTTI}}
\DoxyCodeLine{88 \}}

\DoxyCodeLine{93 \textcolor{comment}{// type.  This can be used as a compile-\/time assertion to ensure that}}
\DoxyCodeLine{94 \textcolor{comment}{// two types are equal.}}

\DoxyCodeLine{103 }
\DoxyCodeLine{104 \textcolor{comment}{// A unique type used as the default value for the arguments of class}}
\DoxyCodeLine{105 \textcolor{comment}{// template Types.  This allows us to simulate variadic templates}}
\DoxyCodeLine{106 \textcolor{comment}{// (e.g. Types<int>, Type<int, double>, and etc), which C++ doesn't}}
\DoxyCodeLine{107 \textcolor{comment}{// support directly.}}
\DoxyCodeLine{108 \textcolor{keyword}{struct }None \{\};}
\DoxyCodeLine{109 }
\DoxyCodeLine{110 \textcolor{comment}{// The following family of struct and struct templates are used to}}
\DoxyCodeLine{111 \textcolor{comment}{// represent type lists.  In particular, TypesN<T1, T2, ..., TN>}}
\DoxyCodeLine{112 \textcolor{comment}{// represents a type list with N types (T1, T2, ..., and TN) in it.}}
\DoxyCodeLine{113 \textcolor{comment}{// Except for Types0, every struct in the family has two member types:}}
\DoxyCodeLine{114 \textcolor{comment}{// Head for the first type in the list, and Tail for the rest of the}}
\DoxyCodeLine{115 \textcolor{comment}{// list.}}
\DoxyCodeLine{116 }
\DoxyCodeLine{117 \textcolor{comment}{// The empty type list.}}
\DoxyCodeLine{118 \textcolor{keyword}{struct }Types0 \{\};}
\DoxyCodeLine{119 }
\DoxyCodeLine{120 \textcolor{comment}{// Type lists of length 1, 2, 3, and so on.}}
\DoxyCodeLine{121 }
\DoxyCodeLine{122 \textcolor{keyword}{template} <\textcolor{keyword}{typename} T1>}
\DoxyCodeLine{123 \textcolor{keyword}{struct }Types1 \{}
\DoxyCodeLine{124   \textcolor{keyword}{typedef} T1 Head;}
\DoxyCodeLine{125   \textcolor{keyword}{typedef} Types0 Tail;}
\DoxyCodeLine{126 \};}
\DoxyCodeLine{127 \textcolor{keyword}{template} <\textcolor{keyword}{typename} T1, \textcolor{keyword}{typename} T2>}
\DoxyCodeLine{128 \textcolor{keyword}{struct }Types2 \{}
\DoxyCodeLine{129   \textcolor{keyword}{typedef} T1 Head;}
\DoxyCodeLine{130   \textcolor{keyword}{typedef} Types1<T2> Tail;}
\DoxyCodeLine{131 \};}
\DoxyCodeLine{132 }
\DoxyCodeLine{133 \textcolor{keyword}{template} <\textcolor{keyword}{typename} T1, \textcolor{keyword}{typename} T2, \textcolor{keyword}{typename} T3>}

\DoxyCodeLine{135   \textcolor{keyword}{typedef} T1 Head;}
\DoxyCodeLine{136   \textcolor{keyword}{typedef} Types2<T2, T3> Tail;}

\DoxyCodeLine{712 }
\DoxyCodeLine{713 \}  \textcolor{comment}{// namespace internal}}
\DoxyCodeLine{714 }
\DoxyCodeLine{715 \textcolor{comment}{// We don't want to require the users to write TypesN<...> directly,}}
\DoxyCodeLine{716 \textcolor{comment}{// as that would require them to count the length.  Types<...> is much}}
\DoxyCodeLine{717 \textcolor{comment}{// easier to write, but generates horrible messages when there is a}}
\DoxyCodeLine{718 \textcolor{comment}{// compiler error, as gcc insists on printing out each template}}
\DoxyCodeLine{719 \textcolor{comment}{// argument, even if it has the default value (this means Types<int>}}
\DoxyCodeLine{720 \textcolor{comment}{// will appear as Types<int, None, None, ..., None> in the compiler}}
\DoxyCodeLine{721 \textcolor{comment}{// errors).}}
\DoxyCodeLine{722 \textcolor{comment}{//}}
\DoxyCodeLine{723 \textcolor{comment}{// Our solution is to combine the best part of the two approaches: a}}
\DoxyCodeLine{724 \textcolor{comment}{// user would write Types<T1, ..., TN>, and Google Test will translate}}
\DoxyCodeLine{725 \textcolor{comment}{// that to TypesN<T1, ..., TN> internally to make error messages}}
\DoxyCodeLine{726 \textcolor{comment}{// readable.  The translation is done by the 'type' member of the}}
\DoxyCodeLine{727 \textcolor{comment}{// Types template.}}
\DoxyCodeLine{728 \textcolor{keyword}{template} <\textcolor{keyword}{typename} T1 = internal::None, \textcolor{keyword}{typename} T2 = internal::None,}
\DoxyCodeLine{729     \textcolor{keyword}{typename} T3 = internal::None, \textcolor{keyword}{typename} T4 = internal::None,}

\DoxyCodeLine{1622 \textcolor{preprocessor}{\# define GTEST\_TEMPLATE\_ template <typename T> class}}
\DoxyCodeLine{1623 }
\DoxyCodeLine{1624 \textcolor{comment}{// The template "{}selector"{} struct TemplateSel<Tmpl> is used to}}
\DoxyCodeLine{1625 \textcolor{comment}{// represent Tmpl, which must be a class template with one type}}
\DoxyCodeLine{1626 \textcolor{comment}{// parameter, as a type.  TemplateSel<Tmpl>::Bind<T>::type is defined}}
\DoxyCodeLine{1627 \textcolor{comment}{// as the type Tmpl<T>.  This allows us to actually instantiate the}}
\DoxyCodeLine{1628 \textcolor{comment}{// template "{}selected"{} by TemplateSel<Tmpl>.}}
\DoxyCodeLine{1629 \textcolor{comment}{//}}
\DoxyCodeLine{1630 \textcolor{comment}{// This trick is necessary for simulating typedef for class templates,}}
\DoxyCodeLine{1631 \textcolor{comment}{// which C++ doesn't support directly.}}
\DoxyCodeLine{1632 \textcolor{keyword}{template} <GTEST\_TEMPLATE\_ Tmpl>}
\DoxyCodeLine{1633 \textcolor{keyword}{struct }TemplateSel \{}
\DoxyCodeLine{1634   \textcolor{keyword}{template} <\textcolor{keyword}{typename} T>}
\DoxyCodeLine{1635   \textcolor{keyword}{struct }Bind \{}
\DoxyCodeLine{1636     \textcolor{keyword}{typedef} Tmpl<T> type;}
\DoxyCodeLine{1637   \};}
\DoxyCodeLine{1638 \};}
\DoxyCodeLine{1639 }
\DoxyCodeLine{1640 \textcolor{preprocessor}{\# define GTEST\_BIND\_(TmplSel, T) \(\backslash\)}}
\DoxyCodeLine{1641 \textcolor{preprocessor}{  TmplSel::template Bind<T>::type}}
\DoxyCodeLine{1642 }
\DoxyCodeLine{1643 \textcolor{comment}{// A unique struct template used as the default value for the}}
\DoxyCodeLine{1644 \textcolor{comment}{// arguments of class template Templates.  This allows us to simulate}}
\DoxyCodeLine{1645 \textcolor{comment}{// variadic templates (e.g. Templates<int>, Templates<int, double>,}}
\DoxyCodeLine{1646 \textcolor{comment}{// and etc), which C++ doesn't support directly.}}
\DoxyCodeLine{1647 \textcolor{keyword}{template} <\textcolor{keyword}{typename} T>}
\DoxyCodeLine{1648 \textcolor{keyword}{struct }NoneT \{\};}
\DoxyCodeLine{1649 }
\DoxyCodeLine{1650 \textcolor{comment}{// The following family of struct and struct templates are used to}}
\DoxyCodeLine{1651 \textcolor{comment}{// represent template lists.  In particular, TemplatesN<T1, T2, ...,}}
\DoxyCodeLine{1652 \textcolor{comment}{// TN> represents a list of N templates (T1, T2, ..., and TN).  Except}}
\DoxyCodeLine{1653 \textcolor{comment}{// for Templates0, every struct in the family has two member types:}}
\DoxyCodeLine{1654 \textcolor{comment}{// Head for the selector of the first template in the list, and Tail}}
\DoxyCodeLine{1655 \textcolor{comment}{// for the rest of the list.}}
\DoxyCodeLine{1656 }
\DoxyCodeLine{1657 \textcolor{comment}{// The empty template list.}}
\DoxyCodeLine{1658 \textcolor{keyword}{struct }Templates0 \{\};}
\DoxyCodeLine{1659 }
\DoxyCodeLine{1660 \textcolor{comment}{// Template lists of length 1, 2, 3, and so on.}}
\DoxyCodeLine{1661 }

\DoxyCodeLine{1665   \textcolor{keyword}{typedef} Templates0 Tail;}
\DoxyCodeLine{1666 \};}

\DoxyCodeLine{2420 \};}
\DoxyCodeLine{2421 }
\DoxyCodeLine{2422 }
\DoxyCodeLine{2423 \textcolor{comment}{// We don't want to require the users to write TemplatesN<...> directly,}}
\DoxyCodeLine{2424 \textcolor{comment}{// as that would require them to count the length.  Templates<...> is much}}
\DoxyCodeLine{2425 \textcolor{comment}{// easier to write, but generates horrible messages when there is a}}
\DoxyCodeLine{2426 \textcolor{comment}{// compiler error, as gcc insists on printing out each template}}
\DoxyCodeLine{2427 \textcolor{comment}{// argument, even if it has the default value (this means Templates<list>}}
\DoxyCodeLine{2428 \textcolor{comment}{// will appear as Templates<list, NoneT, NoneT, ..., NoneT> in the compiler}}
\DoxyCodeLine{2429 \textcolor{comment}{// errors).}}
\DoxyCodeLine{2430 \textcolor{comment}{//}}
\DoxyCodeLine{2431 \textcolor{comment}{// Our solution is to combine the best part of the two approaches: a}}
\DoxyCodeLine{2432 \textcolor{comment}{// user would write Templates<T1, ..., TN>, and Google Test will translate}}
\DoxyCodeLine{2433 \textcolor{comment}{// that to TemplatesN<T1, ..., TN> internally to make error messages}}
\DoxyCodeLine{2434 \textcolor{comment}{// readable.  The translation is done by the 'type' member of the}}
\DoxyCodeLine{2435 \textcolor{comment}{// Templates template.}}
\DoxyCodeLine{2436 \textcolor{keyword}{template} <GTEST\_TEMPLATE\_ T1 = NoneT, GTEST\_TEMPLATE\_ T2 = NoneT,}
\DoxyCodeLine{2437     GTEST\_TEMPLATE\_ T3 = NoneT, GTEST\_TEMPLATE\_ T4 = NoneT,}
\DoxyCodeLine{2438     GTEST\_TEMPLATE\_ T5 = NoneT, GTEST\_TEMPLATE\_ T6 = NoneT,}
\DoxyCodeLine{2439     GTEST\_TEMPLATE\_ T7 = NoneT, GTEST\_TEMPLATE\_ T8 = NoneT,}
\DoxyCodeLine{2440     GTEST\_TEMPLATE\_ T9 = NoneT, GTEST\_TEMPLATE\_ T10 = NoneT,}
